                        <span style="padding-left: 5px;">
                            <strong style="font-size:15pt;">Aaron Sanchez</strong></span>

                    <tr style="background-color: #FFF;"><td style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; font-size:10pt;"><div style="padding-top:5px; padding-bottom:5px; padding-left:5px; padding-right:5px;"><b><a href="http://www.rotowire.com/users/ad_jump.asp?id=688&playerid=11452" style="text-decoration:none;">RotoWire News</a>:</b> Sanchez (1-2) pitched six innings Friday, allowing one unearned run on seven hits and two walks while striking out four Tigers in a road win.                 <tr id="so1" style="background-color: #FFF;"><td colspan="5" style="border-top:2px solid #D3D3D3; padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="width:100%; font-size:10pt"><center>Profiles:&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa7" href="javascript:showMoreSO2015();">2015</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa8" href="javascript:showMoreSO2016();">2016</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;<a id="soa9"  href="javascript:showMoreSO2017();">2017</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;(Click Year to Expand / <a href="javascript:hideSO('so1');">Close</a>)</center></div></td></tr>
                
                
                
                
                
                <tr id="so7" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Sanchez has a sturdy 6-foot-4 / 200 pound frame and loose arm that helped him go in the sandwich round in 2010 out of a southern California high school. He was a raw pitcher with flashes of power stuff, but Sanchez has really grown into his velocity since then, sitting 95-98 and hitting 99 mph in 33 big league relief innings at the end of 2014. As his off-speed stuff has improved to give Sanchez at least mid-rotation stuff, the question remains if he fits better there or as a closer. Toronto’s fifth starter spot is still an open competition along with at least one bullpen slot, so Sanchez has the opportunity this year to prove where he fits. (Kiley McDaniel)</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so8" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>Drafted by Toronto in the sandwich round of the 2010 draft, the hopes were that Aaron Sanchez and his long, lanky body with an electric fastball could develop into an impact starter. That's the hope with most all young pitchers, really. Sanchez debuted as a dominant reliever in 2014, and so Sanchez was tried as a starter to begin 2015. It didn't go well. Sanchez lost a couple ticks off his fastball -- to be expected in a transition to the rotation -- but more troubling was the drop in strikeouts, and the lack of command or control. Sanchez struck out just 42 batters in 66 innings as a starter, and walked an alarming 37. Nothing looked right, and so he went back to the bullpen, where he again looked at home. Maybe this is just Sanchez's future. His lanky body leads to some unorthodox mechanics, and his curveball is his only secondary offering. Sanchez may never be a starter, but that doesn't mean he can't be a dominant reliever. He's now got a 1.67 ERA and a 2.93 FIP in 59 career innings out of the bullpen, and that's where he'll start 2016. Toronto's late offseason acquisition of Drew Storen pushed Sanchez further down the depth chart, though, so Sanchez is likely third in line for saves, at best. (<a href="https://twitter.com/AugustFG_">August Fagerstrom</a>)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>Sanchez flunked his audition as a starter, perhaps reaffirming the notion of many that his future was in a bullpen. No worries. Sanchez looks like a potential dominant relief weapon, though his path to saves in 2016 is foggy.</td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
                <tr id="so9" style="background-color: #FFF; display:none;"><td colspan="5" padding:3px; text-align:justify;"><div class="m_stories" style="font-size:10pt"><center><table><tr><td style="width:615px; padding-right:7px; text-align:justify;" valign="top"><b>Profile: </b>The reigning AL ERA king heads into the 2017 season unshackled by innings limits, and poised to lead the Blue Jays rotation. Sanchez lowered his Deserved Run Average, Earned Run Average, and Fielding Independent Pitching between 2015 and 2016, while maintaining his great Stuff - in the top 5% of all pitchers. He also increased his K/9 by nearly 2 per inning, while cutting his walk rate in half. 2016 was Sanchez's first full season as a starter, and he adjusted his pitching strategy by increasing his command (called strikes above average) from the 2nd %ile, to the 14th %ile, while keeping the ball out of the zone (as indicated by strike probability) more frequently. This is a sure sign that Sanchez is "learning to pitch", all the while, maintaining his elite fastball velocity and movement. The rumours out of Blue Jays camp, are that Sanchez is working on refining his change up, with assistance from Marco Estrada. If there was one knock on Aaron Sanchez in 2016, it was his inability to strike batters out (only a 7.5 K/9). Moving into 2017, the evidence points to him improving on this measure. In 2017, you can expect Sanchez to make a strong case to retain his ERA crown, while providing above average strikeouts, and close to 200 innings. (Mike Sonne)<br /><br /><b>The Quick Opinion: </b>All signs point to Sanchez being a break out star in 2017. With no innings restrictions in place, expect Sanchez to contend for the ERA crown once again, while having a low ERA and average to average+ strikeouts. </td></tr></table></center></div></td></tr>
            </table>
